Title: Speeches at the Second Session of the First National People's Congress
Author: 
Date: 1955-07-28
Page: 3

**Xinhua News Agency, Beijing, July 28th**

**Speech by Minister Liang Xi at the Second Session of the First National People's Congress**

I fully agree with the report by Vice Premier Li Fuquan on the development of the national economy's first five-year plan, the report by Vice Premier Li Xiannian on the 1954 national budget and the 1955 national budget, the report by Vice Premier Deng Zihui on the comprehensive plan for controlling the Yellow River's flood and developing its water resources, the report by Vice Premier Peng Dehuai on the draft of the Military Service Law, and the report by Vice Chairman Peng Zhen on the work of the Standing Committee. I would like to present some opinions on how to achieve the five-year plan for forestry and request the guidance of all representatives!

Forests can conserve water and soil, ensure agricultural water supply, and provide the necessary timber for industry, mining, transportation, construction, and other basic construction needs. If forestry construction cannot keep up with the development needs of industry, agriculture, and other construction projects, it will inevitably affect the overall development of the national economy. This shows that forestry construction is an indispensable and important part of the national economic development plan. However, forestry construction is a long-term and arduous task. Only by relying on the relevant regional party and government leaders and the broad masses, and by doing a good job in the following aspects, can we smoothly achieve the five-year plan for forestry.

(1) Further strengthen the protection of existing forests, especially fire prevention: Due to the insufficient forest resources in our country and the slow growth of trees, in addition to accelerating afforestation, it is more important to protect existing forests. In recent years, we have learned a serious lesson in this regard: to protect forests well, we must rely on the masses under the attention and leadership of local party and government, organize the masses, and tirelessly fight against forest fires and pests. Fire is the greatest enemy of forests. Since liberation until 1953, although forest fires have gradually decreased, in 1954 they increased again, and this spring the situation has become more severe. Some regions have paid great attention to forest fire prevention, and under the unified leadership of the party and government, forest fire prevention has been included in the rural work plan. During periods when mountain fires are likely to occur, provinces, counties, and districts in forest areas all have forest fire prevention command departments; villages and hamlets in forest areas all have forest protection teams; agricultural production cooperatives and mutual aid teams all have forest protection small groups. Everyone, regardless of gender or age, is mobilized to implement a strict piece-by-piece responsibility system, stand guard, and supervise each other. Once a fire occurs, the leading cadres immediately lead the team to extinguish it. In these regions, the spirit of actively preventing and extinguishing fires has become a habit and custom of the local people. However, some regions are complacent and do not understand the spirit of prevention being better than firefighting. They do not supervise and inspect the forest protection organizations of the masses, allowing them to drift; some even think that private forests are not worth protecting and adopt an indifferent attitude. This is extremely wrong. The causes of fires are many, and a considerable part of them are due to the sabotage of counter-revolutionary elements. This cannot but make the party and government in the mountainous areas pay serious attention. In the future, how to heighten vigilance and further organize the masses in the mountainous areas to eliminate all hidden enemies is a necessary and important measure that must be taken for forest fire prevention, and it should also be regarded as an aspect of the complex and long-term class struggle at present. Some fires occur due to the carelessness of the masses in burning fields and clearing land. Due to our inadequate leadership of the mass forest protection organizations, insufficient education of the masses on forest protection, and unclear instructions to the grassroots cadres on the policy of combining forest protection with the production interests of the mountainous areas, burning fields and clearing land have also become an important cause of forest fires. This is extremely inappropriate. Everyone knows that forest areas are mostly sparsely populated and have inconvenient transportation. Once a fire occurs, firefighters cannot arrive in time, often causing serious losses. Based on the experience gained over the past few years, in the future, to prevent fires, in large state-owned forest areas, in addition to relying on the people around the forest areas for protection, the state must also establish some corresponding specialized institutions for management, more importantly, build main roads, equip armed forest protection troops and police stations, and prepare horses and cars. With fire, fight fire; without fire, prevent fire. Search the mountains and forests to prevent spies. In normal times, the forest protection troops can build roads, build watchtowers, and do afforestation and renewal work. In this way, forest fire prevention outside the forest areas can be closely combined with fire prevention inside the forest areas. In the southern private forest areas, where the population is denser than in the border areas, the method of leading by circumstances and adapting to local conditions can be adopted to organize the farmers and implement forest fire prevention, and properly arrange the production in the forest areas. Winter and spring seasons should prohibit burning fields and clearing land. In places where it must be burned, specific places and times should be designated, and organized, led, and guarded burning should be conducted. In short, whether it is state-owned forests or private forests, forest protection work needs everyone to participate.

(2) Actively carry out the planning work in mountainous areas: Vice Premier Li Fuquan's report on the five-year plan says: "In mountainous areas, appropriate unified planning should be carried out to make the development of agriculture, animal husbandry, forestry, and sideline industries of farmers mutually complementary, develop diversified economies, and strengthen water and soil conservation work." This is very important. Only by implementing such planning can the contradictions between agriculture, forestry, and animal husbandry be resolved, can afforestation be promoted in mountainous areas, and can land be fully, effectively, and rationally utilized to gradually prosper the economy of mountainous areas. Based on the planning experience of counties such as Zhejiang's Kaihua, Shandong's Pingyi, and Shanxi's Pingyao, it is estimated that after two or three five-year plans, the economic development level of mountainous areas can be increased by more than two times, and the development potential will be inexhaustible.

Implementing such planning can also avoid the continuous deforestation of mountains. Recently, due to the need for increased grain production, some areas in Jiangxi, Hubei, and Zhejiang provinces are developing large-scale farmland on the mountains. If this is allowed to continue blindly and without planning, it will violate the principles of water and soil conservation and bring long-term and serious disasters to the state and the people. Because every year the mountains are cultivated, coupled with the indiscriminate felling of forests, the soil on the mountains will lose its cover, and a large amount of it will flow into rivers, silt up the rivers, and fill up the riverbeds, causing terrible disasters to the farmland in the plains. In the future, to stop the indiscriminate cultivation, in steep slopes and areas where water and soil are easily lost, strict prohibition of cultivation should be implemented. In areas suitable for cultivation, cultivation should also follow the principles of water and soil conservation, and at the same time, to combine the current interests of the masses with long-term interests, it is necessary to rationally utilize the land and appropriately divide the areas suitable for cultivation, grazing, and forestry. In summary, mountain area production planning must be implemented.

We hope that within the first five-year plan, or a little more time, except for some ethnic minority areas and sparsely populated remote mountainous areas, each province can basically complete the mountain area production planning work. In the southern private forest areas, it is also necessary to combine production planning to investigate and clarify forest resources to strengthen the leadership of private forest afforestation work. These mountain area production planning works must be led by the party and government in a unified manner, must be coordinated by relevant departments, must be carried out on the basis of developing mutual aid and cooperation, and must organize a certain amount of technical force, that is, everyone must participate.

(3) Continue to mobilize the masses to plant trees on a large scale: In recent years, various regions have relied on the masses to plant trees and have achieved great results. For example, in 1954, the area of trees planted by the masses accounted for 94.4% of the total area of trees planted in the country, and among the trees planted by the masses, cooperative afforestation accounted for 70% to 80% of the proportion. Some provinces, such as Shanxi, Anhui, and Hebei, even reached more than 90%. In the first five-year plan, 444.9 thousand hectares of economic forests and 156.2 thousand hectares of protective forests will be planted, with a total area of 601.1 thousand hectares of trees planted. We believe that with the increasing enthusiasm of the masses for socialism and patriotism and the development of mutual aid and cooperation, we can complete and even overfulfill this task.

With the development of cooperative afforestation, various cooperative afforestation organizations have been established nationwide, such as forestry mutual aid groups, forestry cooperatives, agricultural and forestry production cooperatives, or agricultural, forestry, and animal husbandry production cooperatives. By the end of May this year, according to the statistics of 17 provinces, the total number of various cooperative afforestation organizations (not the existing timber cooperatives) has reached 182,000. We hope that the relevant regional party and government will lead these organizations more actively to further consolidate and improve them. Especially in the agricultural production mutual aid and cooperative organizations in mountainous areas, afforestation work should be included in the annual production plan and ensure the completion of the tasks according to the plan. This is also a task that requires everyone to participate.

(4) Steadily promote the work of closing mountains for afforestation: Many facts have proven that closing mountains for afforestation is indeed the most effective and economical way to eliminate barren mountains and conserve water and soil. Over the past five years, various provinces have afforested many mountainous areas through this method, achieving the effects of water storage and soil conservation, and solving part of the fuel and fodder problems for the masses. For example, the Shandong's Yimeng Mountain area, Hebei's Laiyuan County, and Hangzhou's Lingyin Mountain, after planned mountain closure, the slopes are covered with weeds and young trees, and the forests are filled with fallen leaves and humus. In the past, during the rainy season, mountain floods would occur, carrying mud and sand down the mountains. Now this phenomenon has changed, and some places have restored the cultivated land that was washed away. In addition, after closing mountains for afforestation, fruits can be harvested, firewood can be collected, and in some places, oak silkworms can be raised. The benefits are numerous.

However, if the work of closing mountains for afforestation is not done well, it is easy to conflict with the current interests of the masses, and appropriate measures must be taken: (1) There must be unified leadership from the party and government, through mountain area production planning, reasonably divide the forest land, grazing land, and firewood collection areas within a village or township, and establish some necessary and simple-to-operate systems; (2) It must be decided through the township people's congress; (3) It is necessary to carry out continuous propaganda and education to make the closure of mountains for afforestation a collective cause of a village or township, and if necessary, a village or inter-village agreement should be established. This also requires everyone to participate.

(5) Strengthen the management of timber logging in private forest areas: There are many private forests in the southern regions. In recent years, farmers have indiscriminately felled trees, not only exceeding the state's procurement plan every year but also seriously affecting water and soil conservation. For example, the procurement plan for private forests in 1954 exceeded the plan by 40%. According to the repeated suggestions of Soviet experts, it is believed that the forests in the south are basically water source forests. To conserve water sources and conserve water and soil, it is currently advisable to plant more and log less. We believe this suggestion is correct. Therefore, how to limit the indiscriminate logging of farmers through state timber procurement, gradually bring private forest timber production under state planning, is one of the tasks of socialist transformation in rural areas. To achieve the above goals, the following measures must be taken:

(1) Correctly and reasonably adjust the timber prices in various regions, correct the shortcomings of being too high or too low, and use price policies to gradually guide agricultural and forestry production into state planning. (2) Publicize the state's policy of firmly protecting the labor achievements of farmers, as long as they are planted by themselves or obtained during land reform, the state will protect their ownership according to law, so that they can manage their forests with peace of mind and not indiscriminately fell trees. (3) Implement contract procurement. Various levels of party and government should, based on the timber procurement tasks assigned by the state, formulate possible production logging plans, submit them to the forest area township people's congress for discussion, and let the farmers report and discuss the logging quantities of mutual aid groups, cooperatives, and individual farmers, and not log indiscriminately. The procurement stations should, in addition to procuring according to the contract, also prepare a certain amount to procure the timber of individual farmers.

(4) The forest industry institutions and forestry administrative departments should respectively provide technical guidance to farmers in logging, manufacturing, transportation, and afforestation and renewal. (5) Banks and credit cooperatives should, through savings and loans, absorb the idle funds of farmers to engage in forestry and other production. (6) Forest area supply and marketing cooperatives should strengthen the supply of production materials and daily necessities for farmers. This also requires everyone to participate.

(6) Practice thrift and oppose waste: This issue has been seriously raised in the reports of Vice Premier Li Fuquan and Vice Premier Li Xiannian. Here, we have many problems, especially in the timber industry. Although the timber industry has completed the tasks for the state over the past few years and accumulated funds, the phenomenon of waste is serious. This is mainly manifested in: In logging, only good timber is logged, bad timber is not logged, mother trees are not seriously preserved, and logging sites are not cleaned up to create conditions for natural regeneration, causing great damage to forest resources. In basic construction, the standards for building houses are too high. In forest areas where flat houses can be built, some forest industry bureaus in Northeast China prefer to imitate the style of cities and build multi-story buildings and heating systems; each forest industry bureau has a hall, and some halls are decorated quite luxuriously. Although forest railways are production-oriented, some of them also have high design standards. The machines purchased have not been fully utilized. In personnel use, there are too many non-production personnel, and the phenomenon of too many people for too few jobs is serious; absenteeism is also too much. For example, the Yichun Management Bureau had 770,000 man-days of absenteeism last year, and the Harbin Management Bureau had 990,000 man-days of absenteeism last year. In timber storage, according to incomplete statistics of 15 timber yards in Northeast China and Inner Mongolia, due to poor management, among the 27.2 million cubic meters of timber currently in the timber yards, 3.2 million cubic meters have deteriorated and degraded due to pests and rot. To overcome these serious waste phenomena, we are drafting a thrift plan, significantly reducing non-production personnel, and drafting new regulations to lower the standards and costs of basic construction. In the future, in addition to our strict supervision of the thrift of forestry and timber industry institutions in various places, we also hope that various levels of party and government and all representatives will strictly supervise, criticize, expose, and criticize these waste behaviors. That is to say, here, we also hope that everyone will participate. In the past few days, everyone has enthusiastically discussed the first five-year plan for the development of the national economy of the People's Republic of China. Five years is a very short time in forestry. China has so many barren mountains, and trees take so long to grow. The red pines and larches in the Greater and Lesser Xing'an Mountains take 100 to 140 years to grow into large timber, and the firs south of the Yangtze River also need to be cultivated for more than 30 years before they are useful. In just five years, not much work can be done. But five years is the beginning of fifty years or a hundred years. Today, we have learned some experience, discovered boundless strength, and realized that forestry is an indispensable and important part of the overall national economic construction. Under the leadership of the Communist Party of China and Chairman Mao, from the party and government leadership organs to the masses, from the central to the local, everyone participates in the construction of forestry. I believe that we will definitely be able to complete China's first five-year plan and step onto the bright and great road of socialism.

**Speech by Representative Chen Qiyou**

I fully agree with the report by Vice Premier Li Fuquan on the development of the national economy's first five-year plan, the report by Vice Premier Li Xiannian on the 1954 national budget and the 1955 national budget, the report by Vice Premier Peng Dehuai on the draft of the Military Service Law of the People's Republic of China, the report by Vice Premier Deng Zihui on the comprehensive plan for controlling the Yellow River's flood and developing its water resources, and I am determined to strive for their realization! I agree with the report by Vice Chairman Peng Zhen on the work of the Standing Committee of the National People's Congress.

The first five-year plan for the development of the national economy of our country is not only of great historical significance to our country but also of great significance to the world. Due to the reality of the first five-year plan itself, this plan is completely possible to be successfully completed. Naturally, there will be some difficulties in implementation (as pointed out by Vice Premier Li Fuquan), but under the wise leadership of the Communist Party of China and Chairman Mao, plus the enthusiasm and creativity of the Chinese people for socialist construction and the selfless help of the Soviet Union and the support of various people's democratic countries, these difficulties can be overcome.

At the beginning of our liberation, American imperialism and other enemies of the Chinese people had placed their hopes on the crazy idea that the new China would not be able to handle its economy and collapse. But the Communist Party of China and Chairman Mao led us to carry out three years of economic recovery work. By 1952, our national economy had largely recovered to the highest level before the war, and some industrial sectors had even greatly exceeded it; starting from 1953, we began to implement our first five-year plan for construction. After more than two years of practice, we are now able to formulate the plan more realistically and confidently based on reality, and raise some important industrial production to a higher level. History has determined that the people will inevitably win, and what power do the imperialists and all enemies of the Chinese people have to stop the progress of history?

On the other hand, every victory of socialist construction in our country is heartily congratulated by our brother countries and all peace-loving people in the world, because our victory is also their victory; and in the process of implementing the first five-year plan for construction in our country, the active support of the Soviet Union and various people's democratic countries has also become one of the factors for our victory. We should, with the sincerest feelings, thank the Soviet Union, because it is the experience of socialist construction in the Soviet Union that has enabled us to take fewer detours in our construction. With the long-term selfless help of the Soviet Union, we can more confidently complete and overfulfill our construction plan.

The 1954 national budget and the 1955 national budget are in line with our country's great economic construction plan. They have prepared the construction funds for us in a reasonable manner according to our construction steps and stipulated the reasonable expenditure. The 1955 budget clearly indicates the relationship between every unit of income and expenditure and every unit of labor and our national economic construction, and also clearly indicates the direction of our efforts. Completing the state budget is a step forward in the realization of our national economic plan.

In the report on the first five-year plan and the national budget and expenditure report, the issue of increasing production and practicing thrift is specially raised, which is very correct. The huge construction funds needed for socialist construction can only be accumulated from increasing production and saving. However, from past inspections, some funds have been wasted, which is unacceptable. I fully support Vice Premier Li Xiannian's opinion on punishing the behavior of embezzlement and waste. Again, in the 1955 budget, the expenditure for economic construction and social welfare is more than 75%, which strongly proves our country's sincere desire for peace. The slander and defamation of imperialists and all counter-revolutionaries are self-defeating. Finally, I would like to mention a couple of thoughts from my inspection before this meeting: First, after the release of the report on the first five-year plan for the development of the national economy, I heard that some people doubted the increase of grain production in the agricultural sector by only 17.6% compared to 1952. They said that the population growth rate in our country is quite high, and the current grain supply situation is much less than the average rate of rich countries. Therefore, in the first five-year plan, the improvement of the lives of the vast majority of farmers is still very little. I think this view is wrong. Because the characteristic of the first five-year plan for agriculture in our country is to implement the policy of "organizing together." The first five-year plan stipulates that the number of households participating in cooperatives reaches one-third, and further develops and improves various specific forms of labor mutual aid organizations. I myself have inspected the state-owned Nankou Farm and Huangtugang Township Agricultural Production Cooperative near Beijing, and from there, I learned that the income of agricultural production cooperatives is about twice that of when they were still in mutual aid groups, and the income of state-owned farms is about 70% higher than that of cooperatives due to the use of machinery. These two agricultural organizations are still very young and have some shortcomings, but after improvement, they will have greater improvements. This shows that only by gradually bringing agriculture into socialist organizations and implementing agricultural mechanization can income be increased and the lives of farmers be improved. Again, in the first five-year plan, the total value of agriculture and its sideline industries increased by 23.3%, which is not without important significance for improving the lives of farmers. Second, many representatives mentioned the sabotage activities of counter-revolutionaries during the group discussions, which is indeed a serious fact; in coastal areas such as Guangdong Province, because it is adjacent to Hong Kong and Macau, there are more cases of infiltration by American and Kuomintang spies and hidden counter-revolutionaries. During my inspection of the Qinghe Farm labor reform work, I also heard that there was a plot by a former Military Intelligence Bureau spy to organize a riot last year. Combined with the Pan Hannan and Hu Feng incidents, we deeply realize that the sabotage of the enemy is very cunning, and we cannot be complacent. To ensure that our socialist construction is not sabotaged, we must severely suppress all counter-revolutionaries and at the same time strengthen the study of Marxism-Leninism to enhance political vigilance.

I am fully satisfied with the work of the Standing Committee over the past year. The comprehensive plan for controlling and developing the Yellow River, which is valid for fifty years, is a rare giant project in the world. It will transform the river, which is famous for its disasters, to serve the interests of the people. This is something that can only happen in the era of Mao Zedong. I fully support this great plan. I propose that we pass the first five-year plan for the development of the national economy, the 1954 national budget and the 1955 national budget, the Military Service Law of the People's Republic of China, the work report of the Standing Committee, and the comprehensive plan for controlling and developing the Yellow River.

**Speech by Representative Guo Menghe**

I listened to Vice Premier Li Fuquan's report and felt that the first five-year plan is truly great. I fully support it and will resolutely implement it.

I am a drilling worker from the Yumen Oilfield. Since 1945, I have been working there. I am very familiar with the situation in the oilfield before and after liberation. American imperialism and the Kuomintang traitor clique did not want our country to have a petroleum industry at all. During the reactionary rule of the Kuomintang, the Yumen Oilfield operated for more than ten years and was still in ruins. The oilfield had only five small drilling rigs, and each rig could only drill 20 meters per day. A single oil well could drill up to a depth of 800 meters. Only six months of drilling per year. The lives of oil workers were even more miserable. The reactionaries did not treat us as human beings. Living in the Gobi Desert, eating cold rice, many workers got stomach diseases, and even if they were sick, they had no money to treat them.

After liberation, under the leadership of the Communist Party and with the help of the Soviet Union and various people's democratic countries, the situation in the Yumen Oilfield was completely different. Now we have more than 30 large drilling rigs, and we can drill all year round. The daily drilling progress is also improving year by year, and this year we have created a new record of 372 meters per day; and we can drill wells up to 3,000 meters deep. Just in 1954, the number of wells drilled in a single year exceeded the number of wells drilled in more than ten years during the Kuomintang era. Many abandoned wells from before liberation have now been repaired and are producing oil. In the past, American technicians boasted: "Building a Daps coking furnace without three years is not possible, and without Americans is not possible." After liberation, we only took six months to build it. We workers have also become the masters of the oilfield, and our political awareness and production enthusiasm have greatly improved, and our lives have improved a lot. Now we are all working and living happily in the oil city in the Gobi Desert.

The importance of oil is known to everyone. The socialist industrialization and mechanization of agriculture in our country cannot do without oil. Currently, our oil industry is very backward, and the production is far from meeting the demand. The Yumen Oilfield is the first natural oil base in our motherland, and it bears a particularly important responsibility during the first five-year plan. We must strive to do a good job in the reconstruction and expansion, strive to find new oil fields, and increase production to produce more oil to support national construction. There is still a lot of potential in our oilfield. As long as everyone uses their brains and finds ways, it can be tapped. For example, moving a drilling rig used to take seven days, but now it only takes four days, saving the time to drill an average of more than 100 meters, and in the future, it can be shortened even more. Again, take the drilling progress as an example. Although the monthly progress has already reached 800 meters, it is still low compared to the Soviet workers using the same drilling rig to achieve a monthly progress of 1,500 to 2,000 meters, and it can still be improved. The waste in our oilfield is also quite serious. For example, when drilling, only the progress is pursued, regardless of the high cost, and the oil and materials are not cherished, and they are consumed at will. Therefore, we must practice thrift and oppose waste, saving more manpower and money for the state. The youth thrift team in our oilfield has done a good job. They spend one to two hours after work every day, and in more than a month, they have recovered 73 tons of original oil, 35 tons of waste materials, 900,000 bricks, and 10,000 cubic meters of gravel. They have set a good example for all workers.

We want to build, and the enemy will definitely try to infiltrate and sabotage. We have also discovered such incidents in our oilfield. In March, a crane's wire was cut by a counter-revolutionary. In the past, some people thought that there was nothing in the oilfield. In fact, the problem is not that simple. Complacency makes it easy for the enemy to find loopholes. We must all heighten our vigilance, be alert at all times, and eliminate all hidden counter-revolutionaries to prevent the enemy from sabotaging our cause.

I will definitely bring the spirit of this meeting back to convey it clearly to all my fellow workers and, together with all the workers, actively respond to the call of the Party and Chairman Mao to increase production and practice thrift, learn from the advanced experience of the Soviet Union, and ensure the completion of the glorious task assigned to us by the state's first five-year plan.

**Speech by Minister Qian Ying**

I fully agree with the reports by Vice Premiers Li Fuquan, Li Xiannian, Peng Dehuai, Deng Zihui, and Vice Chairman Peng Zhen, and firmly support the draft of the first five-year plan for the development of the national economy of the People's Republic of China.

In the past two years, under the correct leadership of the Central Committee of the Communist Party of China, the Central People's Government, and Chairman Mao, the first five-year plan has been implemented, and our country's industrial and agricultural production has grown rapidly. The national economy has begun to undergo significant changes, and socialist construction and socialist transformation have achieved great success. The political awareness of state workers has been improved. Most of them can faithfully perform their duties, maintain close contact with the masses, maintain a frugal and plain style of work, carry forward the spirit of diligent and conscientious service to the people, and create many heroic and model deeds. This is a powerful guarantee for the realization of China's first five-year plan.

However, in the past two years of implementing socialist construction and socialist transformation, it has also been proven that class struggle is more acute, complex, and profound. This acute and complex struggle is not only manifested in the fact that domestic and foreign enemies have adopted all kinds of despicable and vicious methods to sabotage our construction, but also in the fact that feudal remnants and bourgeois ideology have been constantly infiltrating and corrupting the workers in our departments and enterprises, thereby increasing many difficulties and losses for our construction. This is something we must be vigilant about at all times.

In the past two years, various levels of supervisory organs have focused on inspecting certain serious losses and waste phenomena in some state-owned enterprises. Some departments and enterprises, due to the bureaucracy of the leadership and the irresponsibility of the workers, or the lack of planning and blind procurement, or the practice of wide use and narrow procurement, layer upon layer of increasing the plan, have caused serious material accumulation. By the end of 1954 and the beginning of 1955, the supervisory organs of eight industrial departments inspected 300 enterprises, and the accumulation of materials reached 350 million yuan. Some enterprises still have not completely overcome this phenomenon. For example, the thermal power station of the First Automobile Manufacturing Plant only needed 18 tons of quicklime in the second quarter of this year, but when formulating the second quarter plan, it blindly set it at 7,000 tons, which was 380 times the actual demand. This plan was approved by six people, including the station's planning, review, planning department head, supply department head, chief engineer, and station head, until it was discovered by the supply department's planning department during the review and corrected in conjunction with the supervisory room.

Some factories do not pay attention to safety equipment and maintenance work, resulting in serious accidents. For example, the No. 2 boiler of Tianjin National Cotton Mill No. 1 was found to be leaking water as early as 1951, and after repair, it still leaked occasionally. Since February this year, the leakage has increased, and by April, it leaked 1.5 tons per hour. Workers had repeatedly reported this, but the responsible personnel of the power department and the boiler workshop of the mill covered up and arbitrarily changed the maintenance plan, and did not repair it for a long time. The leadership of the mill did not check this, resulting in an explosion accident, injuring and killing 77 workers and civilians, with a direct property loss of 369,000 yuan, the entire mill stopped work for five days, reducing the production of cotton yarn by 890 pieces and cotton cloth by 20,000 pieces, affecting the completion of the yarn and cloth production plan of the Textile Industry Department in April.

Some industrial and mining enterprises pursue production value and quantity one-sidedly, neglect quality, and do not seriously implement operating procedures and learn from Soviet experience, resulting in the production of a large number of defective products, causing great losses. For example, it was recently found that the Shenyang Heavy Machinery Factory produced 2,800 tons of defective products in 1954, with a net loss of 152,500 yuan, and affected the production and construction of 89 sister factories and mines.

Some state-owned companies also have serious problems with the accumulation and loss of goods. In the first half of this year, the supervisory bureaus of 17 provinces and cities inspected 43 companies, and according to incomplete statistics, the accumulated goods were valued at 52,844,450 yuan. There were also 57 units where the goods were spoiled and damaged due to poor management, with a value of 545 million yuan.

The grain department also has serious problems with grain loss due to poor processing and storage management. According to the inspection of 14 county and city grain warehouses by the Liaoning Provincial Supervisory Bureau in the first half of this year, there were 100 million jin of grain with insects, and 18,000 jin of grain that was completely moldy and unfit for consumption. Some units, due to the political complacency of the leadership, neglected security and protection work, resulting in serious losses caused by bad people taking advantage of the situation. In the first three months of 1955, there were 375 cases of grain theft in Hunan Province, with 46,000 jin of grain stolen, and 52 cases of fire, with 154,500 jin of grain burned.

The causes of the above-mentioned many waste and losses are due to the fact that some institutions are not sound, the leadership is negligent in supervision and inspection; some workers have impure work styles and are seriously irresponsible; some are the result of sabotage by reactionary elements. But some people are indifferent to these situations or do not pay attention to them, and even some leaders of departments and enterprises emphasize that the work is busy and the tasks are urgent, and do not investigate the causes of many serious problems in their work, and therefore, it is not easy to discover the attacks from the enemy from all sides. In the past two years, many supervisory organs have inspected the growing phenomena of embezzlement and theft. In 1954, the supervisory rooms of eight financial and economic departments inspected and handled 5,100 embezzlement cases. Most of the embezzlers were retained personnel or newly recruited personnel, some of whom could not resist the temptation of the bourgeoisie, and some were originally from the bourgeoisie and mixed into our state-owned enterprises to steal intentionally. For example, Xu Weizhen, an embezzler from the Harbin Branch of the People's Bank of China, was originally a capitalist who mixed into our state bank and embezzled a large amount of money. From the late stage of the "Three Antis" movement in 1952 to February 1955, there were 110 instances of embezzlement of "Three Antis" refunds, totaling 26,000 yuan, and he brazenly deposited the money in the bank for two years without being discovered because he pretended to be active. He was only caught and the case was solved when he fled in fear. Again, in a supply and marketing cooperative in a certain district in Hubei Province, a merchant mixed in and became the deputy director, and then brought in eight merchants and hooligans to become cadres, embezzling and stealing, engaging in speculation, exploiting farmers, and causing great indignation among the masses.

In the past two years, various local supervisory organs have focused on inspecting the situation of cadres implementing policies in rural areas, indicating that the vast majority of rural cadres, with mutual aid and cooperation as the center, have carried out various arduous tasks such as the production increase movement, production rescue, flood prevention and drought relief, and unified purchase and sale, and have implemented the various policies of the state for the socialist transformation of agriculture. They have always led the masses with their model behavior and selfless spirit, overcome various difficulties, and fought resolutely against natural disasters and class enemies. They have also discovered counter-revolutionary elements and various criminal elements hidden in rural areas. On the one hand, they have used all kinds of tricks to sabotage our socialist transformation of agriculture, and on the other hand, they have disguised themselves as progressive and active, infiltrated mutual aid and cooperative organizations, usurped the power of the grassroots, and carried out various sabotage activities. For example, in Shandong's Zhangyang County, several bandits such as Mao Dexin usurped the power of the township, colluded with landlords, extorted and robbed, raped women, and framed township cadres, causing unrest. Again, in the 10th district of Shandong's Deqing County, the landlord and former Kuomintang soldier Zheng Qingxiang usurped the position of district head, appointed a bloodthirsty hooligan as the township head, sheltered many counter-revolutionaries, persecuted Communist Party members and cadres, and oppressed the masses. Among the lawless and disorderly elements handled by the national supervisory organs in 1954, there were 2,193 people who were engaged in counter-revolutionary sabotage activities.

Due to the heavy workload in rural areas and the bureaucracy of some leading cadres, who do not understand the situation, only give tasks to cadres, do not clearly explain policies and methods, and do not inspect and help after the tasks are assigned, and some rural cadres have poor work styles or low policy level and lack of experience, they often only care about completing the tasks and do not know how to educate the masses, resulting in some phenomena of forced orders. We should mainly educate these cadres patiently, improve their policy and ideological level, and help them correct their shortcomings and errors. But we must strictly distinguish between those who have degenerated and committed lawless and disorderly acts, especially counter-revolutionary saboteurs. Some people, due to a lack of vigilance against the tricks of class enemies, cannot distinguish between the shortcomings and deviations of our cadres in their work and the deliberate sabotage of counter-revolutionary elements, and attribute many serious problems in rural areas caused by the sabotage of the enemy to the account of rural cadres, or exaggerate the errors and shortcomings of a few cadres into the errors and shortcomings of the majority of cadres, and do not see the hard work and selfless dedication of our broad grassroots cadres, which is obviously incorrect.

The supervisory organs at all levels have suggested that the relevant competent departments improve and correct the problems exposed by the above inspections, and for those who have committed minor errors, they are ordered to reflect and correct, and for those who have committed dereliction of duty, they are punished according to discipline and law. But in the past two years, the supervisory organs at all levels still have many shortcomings in their work, and some problems have not been inspected in time, and some inspections have not been handled in time; some complex problems have not been inspected deeply and thoroughly, and sometimes events caused by the sabotage of bad elements are simply regarded as general events of lax institutions, bureaucratic leadership, and irresponsibility of workers, and therefore the problems cannot be thoroughly solved, the bad elements cannot receive the punishment they deserve, and valuable experience and lessons cannot be learned to educate the broad cadres and masses. These shortcomings should be corrected in the future.

To adapt to the requirements of the new stage of class struggle and more effectively oppose bad people and bad deeds to ensure the smooth progress of socialist construction, it is necessary to further strengthen state supervision, fully play the role of supervision, improve the ideological and combative nature of supervision, and under the leadership of the party committees and governments at all levels and with the assistance and support of relevant departments, rely on the broad masses to concentrate on supervising and inspecting the implementation of the economic construction plan, especially the industrial construction plan. To this end, the political, theoretical, and professional level of supervisory workers must be continuously improved, so that they have a clear and firm class stance, sharp political sensitivity, a high sense of responsibility, and a spirit of seeking truth from facts, and can resolutely fight against bourgeois ideology and saboteurs; can resolutely fight against bureaucracy, extravagance and waste, embezzlement and theft, and lawlessness and disorder, to consolidate state discipline and ensure the implementation of the first five-year plan.

**Speech by Minister Huang Jing**

I fully agree with the draft of the first five-year plan for the development of the national economy and the report by Vice Premier Li Fuquan on the five-year plan. I would like to express some opinions on a key issue in the implementation of the five-year plan by the machinery industryâ€”the issue of mastering new technologies.

The industrialization of the state is to gradually transition the national economy, including agriculture, to a modern technological foundation. Modern production technology is mainly the mechanization of the labor process, replacing manual production with machine production. Therefore, to transform the production technology of various economic departments, it is necessary to have a large number of new machine equipment.

In the first five-year plan, about 38% of the total basic construction investment is used to purchase machinery and equipment. In industrial investment, it accounts for about 40%, in agricultural, forestry, and water conservancy investment, it accounts for about 17%, and even in cultural and educational construction investment, it accounts for 10%. These figures show that the machinery industry bears a heavy responsibility in national construction.

The foundation of China's machinery industry is very backward. Before liberation, the machinery factories were basically engaged in repair and assembly work. Even if they manufactured, they could only make some simple and low-technology machines. After liberation, by transforming repair factories into manufacturing factories, expanding small factories into large ones, and building several new factories, the technical level and manufacturing capacity of the machinery industry have been greatly improved. For example, the Beijing First Machine Tool Factory, which was formed by combining more than ten small repair workshops, initially could only manufacture simple products such as water cranes for adding water to trains and small water pumps. After several years of effort, it can now mass-produce Soviet-type universal milling machines. The Shanghai Machine Tool Factory, which was a farm machinery factory of the Kuomintang bureaucratic capital before liberation, was only a sales outlet for surplus agricultural machinery from the United States in name, and it had never manufactured any machinery. Now it has become a factory that manufactures precision grinders. The total output value of the national machinery industry in 1954 has reached 13 times that of 1949, and nearly 2,000 new types of products have been added. At present, we can manufacture more than 70 types of new machine tools, 6,000 kW thermal power generation equipment, 10,000 kW hydropower generation equipment, medium-speed diesel engines, coking equipment, mining exploration, mining, transportation, washing, crushing, and hoisting equipment for one cubic meter of electric shovels, railway locomotives, medium-sized ships, grain combine harvesters, and pneumatic tools, rolling bearings, etc. In the next three years, we will produce and trial-manufacture more than 1,540 new varieties, including about 100 new types of machine tools, 12,000 kW thermal power generation equipment, 3 cubic meter electric shovels, 1,000 cubic meter blast furnace equipment, heavy-duty trucks, and light tractors. These facts show that the supply capacity of the machinery industry is rapidly increasing, but compared to the growth of national needs, it is still far from enough. During the first five-year plan period, the number of machines and equipment needed is only about 60% that can be supplied domestically; in terms of variety, the proportion that can be supplied is even less, and many especially large, special precision, and complex sets of equipment cannot be manufactured during the first five-year plan period. In addition, some of the products we can manufacture are still not up to standard in quality. For example, some machine tools do not meet the specified accuracy, some power machinery does not meet the required efficiency, and some factories, because the quality of the products is not good, often send people to various places to repair the products that have already been shipped. The lack of variety and poor quality are the fundamental problems of the machinery industry at present, and the main reason is our technological backwardness.

First, the technological foundation is backward. To manufacture modern machinery products, a certain level of technological equipment is required. To manufacture large products, large equipment is needed; to manufacture precision products, precision machine tools are needed. To mass-produce complex and precise products, many special equipment is needed. In recent years, although existing enterprises have added a lot of equipment, it is still difficult to manufacture especially large and special precision products. For example, a set of rolling mill equipment with 1,150 millimeters of initial rolling equipment has tens of thousands of parts, and many of these parts are large. Among them, the heaviest part weighs 80 tons, and casting and forging these parts require a large steel casting workshop and heavy forging equipment; processing these parts also requires a set of special heavy machine tools. Therefore, to produce such products in sets, new factories must be built.

Second, the technological strength is weak. Especially high-level technical personnel and high-level skilled workers are not only few in number but also incomplete in their trades. Therefore, many technical institutions that should be established cannot be established; new large factories require many engineers, and we cannot fully equip them; many technical problems in existing factories cannot be solved in time. The design of new factories and the design of products are mostly dependent on the assistance of the Soviet Union and various people's democratic countries, and we cannot yet independently carry out relatively complex designs. In terms of technology, many advanced processing methods, such as precision machining, welding, and large-scale forging, are still difficult to implement.

Third, there are still backward repair habits in production. In recent years, under the direct help of experts sent by the Soviet Union and various people's democratic countries, we have learned some advanced experience, and the organization and technical level of production have been greatly improved. However, in establishing a regular technological system and changing the old repair habits, the extent to which various factories have done so is very uneven. To thoroughly and universally do this work well, we still need to make great efforts. At present, some products do not have a complete set of technical documents, or even if there are technical documents, they still lack the necessary regulations and systems to ensure their implementation. Some products, although they have drawings and standards, are not strictly manufactured according to the drawings and standards, and there is a lack of unified and strict regulations for the production process, the machines, tools, materials, and operating methods that should be used, and some, although there are regulations, have not been strictly implemented. Some workers still habitually use old methods, and each master has their own set of operating methods. In terms of inspection, there is also a lack of clear inspection standards and strict systems. In this way, the parts made cannot be precise, and when assembling, they can only be adjusted by making large ones smaller and small ones larger, using the so-called "matching" and "filing, scraping, hammering, and hitting" methods to assemble them together. The machines made in this way, of course, cannot be of good quality.

The technological backwardness of the machinery industry is obviously not in line with the requirements of national economic development. Without building a powerful machinery industry, it is not possible to achieve socialist industrialization and independently develop the national economy. Therefore, the first five-year plan puts the development of heavy industry as the central link of socialist industrialization and emphasizes the development of the machinery industry, which is completely necessary. Vice Premier Li Fuquan pointed out in the five-year plan report: Improving industrial technology level is a basic condition for completing the task of socialist industrialization. We believe this is completely correct. It is necessary to overcome the technological backwardness of the machinery industry to make the machinery industry develop strongly.

To overcome the technological backwardness of the machinery industry, efforts must be made in two aspects: on the one hand, under the technical assistance of the Soviet Union and various people's democratic countries, build a batch of new modern factories to fundamentally change the backward technological foundation of the machinery industry; on the other hand, carry out technological transformation of the existing factories.

In the five-year plan, the machinery industry will build a batch of new factories, and these factories are equipped with the latest technology. After completion, they will greatly change the face of the machinery industry. This is the most important aspect of overcoming the technological backwardness of the machinery industry. After the new factories are completed, the key issue is the problem of mastering new technologies. Only by mastering new technologies can qualified products be manufactured, and the production capacity of the factory can be fully utilized to meet the requirements of the factory design. To master new technologies, first of all, various preparatory works must be done before starting production. When the various technical documents of a factory designed abroad arrive, they must be quickly organized for translation and carefully studied, and then these documents are used as the basis for various specific preparatory works. Such as personnel, equipment, tools, materials, and external cooperation. These preparatory works must be prepared in full according to the conditions specified in the technical documents before starting production. Next, trial production must be carried out: to test whether the equipment, tools, materials, etc. meet the requirements, to check various technical documents, and to educate the workers to familiarize themselves with and master the new equipment, tools, and operating methods. In the trial production, from parts to finished products, the first requirement is to make them according to the rules (to meet the quality standards), and then to make them fast (to meet the technical quotas), until all processes are mastered, and then it is considered that the new production has been completely mastered.

In the process of mastering new production, the most important thing is to strictly follow the regulations of the technical documents, and to repeatedly educate the workers that they must insist on learning new technologies, actively overcome difficulties, and not arbitrarily change the regulations, and must abide by the technological discipline. Only by cultivating such a regular production habit can a good foundation be laid for formal production in the future; if a bad root is left at this time, it will be difficult to change it later. However, we have shortcomings in this regard. In the past, we lacked a clear understanding of mastering new production, and some comrades thought that being able to produce one or two qualified products meant mastering new production. But how were these one or two qualified products made? They were made under the condition of wasting a lot of labor and materials by using irregular methods. Although these one or two finished products can barely meet the standard, they cannot be produced in batches when formally produced. The Wind Power Tool Factory, which has been put into production, once neglected this point. They did not seriously study and implement the design materials of the Soviet Union and still acted according to their old habits. Although they corrected it later, they had already taken a detour. This is a serious lesson for us. Of course, in the process of trial production, there will be situations where the requirements of the technical documents are not suitable for the specific conditions of our country, and it is necessary to make some necessary modifications, for example, some materials cannot be produced domestically for the time being, and substitute materials must be used. The method of processing and other things must also be changed accordingly. However, such modifications must not be made lightly, and they can only be changed when it is really necessary, and they must be strictly reviewed and approved.

During the first five-year plan period, the number of new factories put into production is not large, and the main reliance is still on the production of existing factories. Moreover, the cultivation of technical strength and the accumulation of technical experience also need to be undertaken by existing factories. Therefore, the technological transformation of existing factories is also an extremely important aspect of changing the technological backwardness of the machinery industry. We cannot only pay attention to the construction of new factories and neglect the transformation of existing factories.

Based on the experience of the past few years, the technological transformation of existing factories mainly involves the following aspects:

First, clarify the professional development direction of the enterprise and organize specialized production. At present, some enterprises have not determined their professional direction, or although they have a professional direction, they have not organized specialized production. Therefore, in these factories, there are many universal machines and few specialized machines, and specialized technical problems cannot be solved. The production efficiency is very low. The professional direction of the enterprise is not clear, so it cannot consider the sequence of product development in a planned manner, and therefore the technical development lacks direction. Not organizing specialized production cannot reasonably organize the production process according to the characteristics of the products, equip specialized equipment and tools, and accumulate specialized design and manufacturing experience and cultivate specialized technical personnel and workers, thus greatly hindering the improvement of the technical level. Therefore, clarifying the professional direction of the enterprise and organizing specialized production is an important prerequisite for the comprehensive technological transformation of old enterprises. The professional direction of each factory must be arranged and decided comprehensively and in detail according to the needs of the state and combined with the specific conditions of each factory. Otherwise, production and needs will not be able to adapt to each other.

Second, it is necessary to appropriately supplement the necessary equipment, tools, and experimental and inspection instruments according to the professional development direction of the enterprise; the old equipment should be fully utilized, and it should be checked and repaired to improve its efficiency and restore its precision, so that the existing enterprises can produce more and better varieties of products, and fully utilize the production capacity.

Third, it is necessary to establish a modern and regular production technical order through the trial production of new products and the technical improvement of old products. The trial production of new products must prepare drawings and necessary technical documents, and in these documents, the technical conditions of the products, the methods of processing and inspection, and the use of what equipment, tools, materials, etc. should be specified, and then the above drawings and various regulations should be tested and identified through trial production, and then formally enter production in a regular manner, and strictly implement the inspection work in production. Unqualified products cannot be shipped. Continuously produced old products should also be improved technically in the same way as new products.

In addition, it is necessary to pay attention to the creation of the masses in technology and not to neglect it because it is necessary to act according to the rules. It is necessary to organize rationalization suggestions under leadership, give full play to the wisdom of the masses, and solve some key problems in technology. The creation of the masses should be scientifically identified and summarized, and then promoted.

To master new technologies, it is also necessary to solve two problems:

First, cultivate technical strength. The cultivation of technical strength requires two aspects: one is training from schools. At present, the frameworks of technical schools at all levels have been established, and the number of graduates will increase year by year in the future, but the general quality is still relatively poor and needs to be improved. On the other hand, it is necessary to develop part-time education. Soviet experience proves that this is the most effective way to cultivate industrial talents. In our current situation where there are many transferred cadres, promoted workers, and new workers, part-time education is even more important.

Second, cultivate independent design capabilities and develop scientific research work. At present, the design of our factories and the design of products are mostly dependent on the assistance of the Soviet Union and various people's democratic countries; but we cannot rely on this indefinitely. In the future, we need to build more new factories, produce more products, and also need to carry out special designs according to the characteristics of our country's resources and special needs, which requires us to have independent design capabilities; and independent design must be based on experimental research work. Therefore, we must strengthen our ties with the research institutions of the Academy of Sciences and universities, and actively establish and strengthen the design and technological research institutions within the department, and carry out technological research work. The above are the main tasks we need to do to master new technologies. To carry out the above work, we must first fully estimate the role of the assistance of the Soviet Union and various people's democratic countries. They not only help us design new factories, supply important equipment, train and train personnel, and provide valuable technical data, but also send their best experts to specifically guide our work, which is a very favorable condition for us to overcome technological backwardness, and we must make full use of this superior condition. Next, the mastery of new technologies cannot be carried out in isolation, but must be combined with the work of all aspects of the enterprise, especially with the improvement of management and the increase of production and savings, and the strengthening of political and ideological work, and the struggle to eliminate hidden counter-revolutionaries, to ensure the completion of our tasks.

In our work, there are many difficulties, but we believe that as long as we follow the instructions of Chairman Mao: earnestly learn from the advanced experience of the Soviet Union and various people's democratic countries, be honest and hardworking, help and encourage each other, and be vigilant against any boasting and arrogance, we will be able to overcome the difficulties and complete the tasks assigned to us by the five-year plan.

**Speech by Representative Cai Tingkai**

I fully agree with the report by Vice Premier Li Fuquan on the development of the national economy's first five-year plan and the report by Vice Premier Li Xiannian on the 1954 national budget and the 1955 national budget.

Our country's first five-year plan for the development of the national economy reflects the will and demands of the entire nation, is centered on the implementation of socialist industrialization, and is formulated based on the general line of the Communist Party of China in the transitional period, that is, the general task of the state in the transitional period. This is a great and unprecedented economic construction plan. This plan has been successfully implemented since 1953 and has already achieved great success and gained valuable experience in the past two years of practice, thereby further guaranteeing that our first five-year plan will definitely be completed and overfulfilled. I sincerely support this plan and will exert all my efforts to implement it.

I deeply realize that the future of our great motherland is to build a brilliant socialist society. The central task of building a socialist society must be to gradually realize the socialist industrialization of the state, and the priority development of heavy industry is the central link of socialist industrialization. The first five-year plan clearly points out this correct policy and emphasizes this correct policy, which is a great help and encouragement to the people's ideological understanding. Our revolutionary teacher Lenin repeatedly instructed: "The only and true foundation for building a socialist society is one, that is, large-scale industry." It is obvious that without heavy industry, we cannot transition to socialism, and we cannot transform agriculture and the entire national economy on the basis of modern technology.

The first five-year plan also elaborates on how to solve the contradictions between small peasant economy and socialist industrialization, and how to solve the contradictions between capitalist economy and socialist economy. These explanations and regulations show that our first five-year plan is such a comprehensive and correct great economic construction plan. The implementation of this great economic construction plan marks the unlimited bright and happy future and beautiful prospect of our great motherland.

In the short three years since liberation, our great motherland has successfully completed the work of restoring the national economy, and it is on this basis of victory that we have the superior conditions to carry out large-scale economic construction. Since 1953, we have achieved many remarkable results in industrial construction, and now the reconstruction and new construction of the Anshan Iron and Steel Combined Enterprise in our country are making rapid progress; the rapid increase in steel production has greatly changed the face of the steel industry. In the machinery manufacturing industry, many factories have been built or are being newly built, such as heavy machinery factories, machine tool factories, wire factories, automobile factories, locomotive factories, tractor factories, etc., all with very large construction scales. In addition, the development of coal, electricity, and petroleum industries has achieved astonishing results. For example, the Fuxin Haizhou open-pit coal mine has completely mechanized production, and an electric shovel can dig 50,000 jin of coal at a time. The 700-mile-long ultra-high-voltage power transmission line in Northeast China can fully supply the power needs of many industrial cities and factory and mine enterprises. The production of the Yumen Oilfield has increased unprecedentedly, and the production in 1953 was nearly two and a half times that of 1949. These facts show that the foundation of our country's heavy industry has gradually and steadily been established. With the development of heavy industry, our country's light industry and transportation industry have also developed accordingly. Agriculture and handicrafts have also organized and moved towards the path of cooperation. Capitalist industry and commerce have gradually moved towards state capitalism through the paths of utilization, restriction, and reform. In the commercial sector, the development of state-owned and cooperative commercial enterprises has guaranteed the implementation of the planned procurement and planned supply policy, ensuring market stability. Due to the rapid progress and remarkable achievements of all these construction projects, in recent years, the material and cultural lives of the people across the country have been continuously improved and improved accordingly. This is a good start for building socialism, the victory fruit of the first two years of implementing the first five-year plan, and thus has gained the unanimous trust and praise of the people across the country. At the same time, it reflects internationally that the achievements of China's economic construction and peaceful foreign policy are increasingly gaining the admiration and sympathy of the people of various countries, with increasing influence and rising international status. In recent years, I have attended the World Peace Council and the World Peace Conference many times and deeply felt that people from various countries have a correct understanding of our country day by day, and have expressed their friendship and deep and cordial tendencies in different ways. Of course, comrades and friends from the Soviet Union and people's democratic countries are even more joyful and inspiring about our construction achievements.

Vice Premier Li Fuquan pointed out in the report: "No matter what aspect of the task of our country's first five-year plan, it is very arduous. In the first five-year plan period, our country is carrying out large-scale construction work on the basis of weak productive forces, which cannot be without difficulties. Our work is very tense. In the past two years, we have overcome many difficulties and completed many arduous and complex tasks, but in the future, we will still encounter various difficulties, and the tasks will be more arduous and complex." This shows that the tasks of the next three years of work are more arduous and complex than the past two years, and the difficulties we will encounter will certainly not be few. Therefore, we must not be satisfied with the situation of the first five-year plan being successfully implemented in the past two years and the achievements it has shown; we must be full of spirit and work even harder for the tasks of the next three years, and make unremitting efforts, so that we can fully complete the five-year plan. In the past two years of work, we must not avoid saying that there were some shortcomings and some mistakes. In the basic construction, especially in the non-production housing construction, there were many and serious waste phenomena. In the implementation of the unified purchase and sale policy of grain, there were also some deviations, more or less. This has brought great losses to the state and the people and has added some difficulties to the implementation of the first five-year plan. However, we have discovered the shortcomings in time and corrected the shortcomings in time; we have discovered the deviations in time and also corrected the deviations in time, so that we can continuously improve and continuously advance through the methods of checking work in time and summarizing experience and lessons in time.

In early February, I went to Guangzhou and attended the second session of the Guangdong Provincial People's Congress. I heard the report of the local administrative chief and also observed the facts with my own eyes. I think that the construction work in various aspects in Guangdong Province has made great progress and development in the past two years. The deviations in the treatment of overseas Chinese relatives during the land reform and the individual shortcomings in the grain procurement have also been checked and corrected, so the people of Guangdong Province are enthusiastically supportive of the measures of the local government. I hope that the working cadres in Guangdong will, in the future, further carry out the intentions of the central government, based on the regulations of the five-year plan, continue to work hard, and complete the tasks of the future work.

At the meeting, I heard Vice Premier Li Xiannian's report on the 1954 national budget and the 1955 national budget, which pointed out that our country has achieved certain results in developing the national economy, improving people's lives, and consolidating national defense forces by realizing the 1954 budget, and the realization of the 1955 national budget will further achieve results in these aspects. Therefore, I feel that this is an exciting and inspiring report. We must ensure that, like 1954, we will successfully realize the 1955 national budget. This will be very beneficial to the completion of the tasks of the five-year plan. I fully agree with the current nationwide efforts to implement the CPC Central Committee and the State Council's instructions to practice thrift and the launch of a mass campaign against waste. Only in this way can we combine the development of production and the increase of income to ensure the complete realization of the 1955 national budget of our country, and thus also ensure the successful completion of the five-year plan, especially the 1955 annual plan.

In the progress of the great cause of socialist construction, I deeply realize that the realization of the five-year plan is a complex and acute class struggle. Domestic and foreign enemies and all counter-revolutionaries will not be willing to die and will inevitably make desperate and cunning struggles. The recent cases of American and Kuomintang spies uncovered and sentenced in Tianjin and Guangdong, as well as other cases of reactionary sectarian organizations uncovered in various places, prove that the enemy is making every effort to attack us and sabotage our construction. The Hu Feng counter-revolutionary clique is an enemy who has infiltrated into our ranks in a hidden and disguised manner. We must heighten our political vigilance, eliminate all hidden counter-revolutionaries, and break through any form of sabotage by domestic and foreign enemies and counter-revolutionaries against the five-year plan. The recent exposure of the Hu Feng counter-revolutionary clique is a major victory in the struggle of the people across the country against counter-revolutionary conspiracies. Our country's first five-year plan is a great plan for the development of the national economy. To ensure the realization of this great five-year plan and to ensure the completion of our country's socialist construction, we must closely unite around the Communist Party of China, faithfully accept the leadership of the Communist Party of China and Chairman Mao Zedong. As Chairman Mao Zedong said:

"We are doing an extremely glorious and great business that our predecessors have never done." The people of the whole country should unite as one, unite together, and strive to complete and overfulfill the first five-year plan!

**Speech by Representative Wang Yilun**

I fully agree with the first five-year plan for the development of the national economy, and I fully agree with the reports by Vice Premiers Li Fuquan, Li Xiannian, Peng Dehuai, and Deng Zihui, and Vice Chairman Peng Zhen to the conference, and I propose that the conference adopt them.

Heilongjiang Province is an important industrial and agricultural region in our country, with rich forest resources. During the first five-year plan period, it bears heavy responsibilities in basic construction, industry, agriculture, and forestry production. In recent years, although we have done some work in industrial construction and achieved certain results, there are still many shortcomings. The problems in industrial construction mentioned by Vice Premiers Li Fuquan and Li Xiannian in their reports exist in Heilongjiang Province, and the criticism of the waste phenomena in some units in Heilongjiang Province is also completely correct. In the future, we must strengthen leadership and supervision to ensure the smooth completion of the state's industrial construction tasks.

Vice Premier Li Fuquan pointed out in the report: Overcoming the contradiction between the development of agriculture lagging far behind the development of industry is a major task of the five-year plan. We deeply feel that in the first five-year plan, Heilongjiang Province has a particularly important responsibility in agriculture. Heilongjiang Province has a vast land area, with about 97.5 million mu of cultivated land, and nearly 1 billion mu of cultivable land; the existing cultivated land has fertile soil, convenient transportation, abundant water sources, and a climate and rainfall suitable for the production of various crops, so the grain yield is abundant, and commercial grain accounts for half of the total yield; if the cultivable land is fully developed, it can increase a large amount of fertile land for the state, equivalent to the cultivated land area of Heilongjiang Province. Due to the vast land and sparse population, the cultivation is relatively rough, and the small peasant economy is still dominant, and a large area of wasteland has not been developed, so the potential of agricultural production is great. We have confidence and will ensure the victory of the agricultural production increase indicators and agricultural cooperativization indicators assigned to our province by the state in the first five-year plan and strive to overfulfill them.

The report of the five-year plan mentions the issues of agricultural cooperativization, agricultural production increase measures, and agricultural leadership, which are also the main issues of Heilongjiang Province's agriculture. After the end of the fallow period last year, the agricultural cooperativization movement in Heilongjiang Province made a great leap forward, with the number of households participating in cooperatives increasing from 7% of the total number of households to 36%. The development of the cooperativization movement is basically normal and healthy, with 95% being consolidated or can be consolidated, and the vast majority can increase production or can increase production through efforts.
