The first five-year plan for the development of the national economy outlines a preliminary picture of our country's march towards prosperity and strength, and its realization will lay a good foundation for our country's socialist industrialization and socialist transformation. This is also a reliable guarantee for the development and progress of the Yi areas. The realization of this plan is the greatest benefit to all ethnic groups in the country, and it is also the greatest benefit to the Yi people. We must make every effort to strive for its realization.

It cannot be said that the five-year plan is only a matter of the Han areas, nor can it be said that the five-year plan has nothing to do with or little to do with the minority areas. In the draft of the five-year plan, according to the different regions where the various ethnic minorities are located and the different conditions they possess, specific regulations have been made to build several railways and highways, establish several mechanized farms, tractor stations, schools, health institutions, and conduct surveys and research on resources and transportation, etc., which are directly related to the development of economic and cultural undertakings in the minority areas (including the Yi areas). Take our West Sichuan Liangshan Yi Autonomous Prefecture as an example. In the past few years, due to the implementation of the Communist Party of China and Chairman Mao's ethnic policy, with the overall development of the country and the strong support of the Han areas, the Liangshan Yi area has made significant progress and development. In political terms, ethnic regional autonomy has been implemented, a group of Yi cadres have grown, and in various levels of power, they mainly manage the affairs of their own ethnic groups; ethnic relations have been greatly improved, many disputes within the Yi ethnic group have been mediated, and many "enemies" have become relatives, and many battlefields for fighting enemies have become markets that meet the needs of the people, and many wastelands have become good fields. In economic terms, in recent years, due to the large amount of investment by the state (only the free distribution of iron agricultural tools has reached more than 400,000 items) and the promotion of advanced cultivation technology, the extremely backward state of "slash-and-burn" has been greatly changed, and both agriculture and animal husbandry have developed. According to the investigation and calculation of key areas, in 1954, the main crops increased by about 40% compared to 1949, and the income from animal husbandry and sideline industries increased by more than one fold, and the purchasing power of the people increased by 2.7 times. The remaining trade and transportation industries have also developed rapidly, and the business volume of state-owned commerce in 1954 increased by 69 times compared to 1951. The autonomous prefecture and various counties have connected the postal roads and wired telephones. In terms of culture and health, most areas have established ethnic primary schools, and each county has a well-equipped health center, health station, and health station, and the disease and death rates of the Yi people have been greatly reduced. Due to the above changes, the Yi people deeply feel the warmth of the big family of the motherland and Chairman Mao's care for ethnic minorities. They say: "The sun only shines during the day, the moon only shines at night, only Chairman Mao is the sun that never sets day and night." From the development and changes of the Yi areas in recent years, it should be understood that only when our entire country develops in all aspects, especially when socialist industrialization develops, can we guarantee that the Yi areas achieve success in all aspects, promote the development of the economy and culture of the Yi areas, and ensure that the minority areas can gradually transition to a prosperous and happy socialist society. Therefore, the realization of the five-year plan is not unrelated to us or has little to do with us, but has a very close relationship. We, the Yi people, must, together with the people of all ethnic groups in the country, strive for the realization of this plan. Although the Liangshan Yi area has made some progress and changes in various aspects in recent years, it is still a very backward area. To eliminate this backward state, to make the work of the Yi area adapt to the requirements of national construction, and to liberate the Yi people thoroughly, we must steadily, resolutely, and actively advance along the socialist road. Those who are satisfied with the status quo, think that "progress" has already been enough, and therefore do not actively work according to objective possible conditions, or do not actively and patiently cultivate and help Yi cadres, or do not actively seek the help of Han cadres, or do not actively develop production, and carry out trade, health, and other work in a passive attitude, are all wrong. These attitudes actually make our various work "stable but not progressive," and will make the Yi area remain in a backward state for a long time, which is not beneficial to the Yi people or national construction. These problems, we often produce ourselves, and we must pay attention to overcoming them. Of course, it is also necessary to prevent and correct the tendency of impetuousness and adventurism that exceeds the objective possible conditions. In short, we, the Yi people, must resolutely and actively walk the socialist road to have a bright future. At present, we should actively prepare the conditions for the implementation of democratic reform, and create more favorable conditions for the development of the economy and culture of the Yi area and the improvement of people's lives. Only in this way can we gradually make the Yi people shake off backwardness and join the ranks of advanced ethnic groups, and gradually transition to a socialist society.

Bo Yibo, Director, spoke:
The development of the national economy's first five-year plan in our country is a major step for the people of the whole country, under the leadership of the Central Committee of the Communist Party of China, Chairman Mao Zedong, and the State Council, to realize the country's overall task in the transitional period. Its thorough implementation will lay the initial foundation for the socialist industrialization of our country. Here, I would like to express some opinions on the development of heavy industry in the five-year plan.

Heavy industry is the industry that produces means of production, and it bears the heavy responsibility of transforming the technological foundation of the national economy and expanding socialist reproduction. The five-year plan stipulates the priority development of heavy industry and uses 88.8% of industrial investment to build heavy industry. I think this is completely in line with the party's general line in the transitional period and the fundamental interests of the people of the whole country. Since liberation, heavy industry has developed greatly, and the annual output of major products, if 1952 is taken as 100, the growth situation in 1954 is as follows: pig iron 156, steel 165, electricity 151, raw coal 126, raw oil 184.1, ammonium sulfate 164.7, cement 161; the output value of machinery products, if calculated by the total production value, is 200% of 1952 in 1954. The growth of product varieties is also very rapid, and the machinery industry has successfully developed nearly 2,000 new products in a few years, and the black and non-ferrous metal industries have successfully developed more than 220 new products in 1954 alone. We can now produce 6,000-kilowatt power generation equipment, 154,000-volt and 20,000-kilovolt-ampere single-phase transformers, lathes with a cutting diameter of up to 5 meters, combined coal mining machines, locomotives, grain combine harvesters, new sets of textile machinery, medium-sized coastal ships and inland river ships. We are currently producing 10,000-kilowatt hydroelectric power generation equipment, blast furnace equipment with a capacity of 1,000 cubic meters, and coking equipment with an annual output of 300,000 tons, etc.

However, compared to the needs of the state, the level of heavy industry is still very backward. In 1955, the planned output of steel is only 3.6 kilograms per person when distributed per capita; especially high-quality steel, large and high-grade alloy steel cannot be produced; the varieties of non-ferrous and rare metals are not many; machinery and equipment can only meet about 60% of the needs of the state, especially large, special precision, and complex sets of products, most of which cannot be manufactured; the supply of electricity and oil is very tight; geological work is lagging behind the requirements of industrial development. Therefore, we must vigorously develop heavy industry. During the five-year plan period, various departments of heavy industry will build a large number of modern new enterprises and renovate existing enterprises; they will smelt hundreds of varieties of high-quality steel; they will manufacture thousands of new products, including those that cannot be manufactured now, and many kinds of heavy machinery and precision machine tools, aircraft, heavy trucks, and tractors, etc. By 1957, the total production value will be increased by 126.5% compared to 1952.

On the basis of the very weak heavy industry, to smoothly complete the above construction and production tasks is a very difficult task, and we must make the greatest efforts to solve the following problems.

First, regarding the technological renovation of heavy industry and the mastery of new technologies

The technological foundation of heavy industry in our country is very backward: the scale of enterprises is small, the equipment is outdated, the development is unbalanced, the degree of mechanization is low, and there is a lack of technical experience. On this backward basis, it is difficult to undertake the task of comprehensively transforming the technological foundation of the national economy. Therefore, in the initial stage of our industrial construction, we must first focus on the technological renovation of heavy industry and strive to gradually improve the technological level of heavy industry in our country to the level that an advanced industrial country should have after several five-year plans, and gradually transform the technological foundation of industry, transportation, and agriculture in our country in a planned and step-by-step manner.

During the first five-year plan period, the 156 new enterprises built by the Soviet Union to help our country are the first step in realizing the technological renovation of heavy industry in our country. These new enterprises have adopted the latest technological equipment and already have an advanced technological foundation. After building and mastering this batch of new enterprises, it will be possible to gradually place heavy industry in our country on the foundation of modern scientific and technological achievements. The main problem in these new enterprises is how to master new technologies, produce products that meet the design requirements in quality, and strive to quickly reach the design capacity. To do this, we must seriously study Soviet technical materials, train technical personnel and workers, learn to use new machinery and equipment, be familiar with the operation methods of new equipment, strictly follow the requirements of advanced design, and master the entire new production process.

Another important aspect of the technological renovation of heavy industry is to adopt and master new technologies in existing enterprises. Various departments of heavy industry should, on the basis of fully utilizing existing equipment, plan to add modern technological equipment according to the needs and possibilities of production development, improve the degree of mechanization of the production process, and gradually replace heavy manual labor with machines. We must strengthen product design, trial production, testing, and inspection work, establish strict technical order, formulate complete technical documents, strengthen process discipline, learn to use new technological equipment and new operation methods, and overcome backward production habits. In this way, we can improve production efficiency, increase the variety of products, and continuously improve product quality.

The adoption and mastery of new technologies must rely on the guidance of scientific and technological research work. For this reason, various departments of heavy industry must establish and improve research and experimental institutions as soon as possible, gradually do so that they can propose the technological development direction of their own departments, and make the formulation of technological policies and the compilation of technological development plans have a basis.

In the process of implementing technological renovation, we must comprehensively learn from the Soviet Union, and we must always summarize and apply all the existing and newly created advanced experiences at home and abroad. This is the basic way to quickly improve the technological level.

Second, carry out the work of industrial standardization

Standardization is an important technological policy in the process of realizing socialist industrialization. Standardization is to make unified regulations for various elements such as raw materials, products, production processes, technical conditions, and quality requirements in industry. Those that need to be implemented nationwide are promulgated as national standards by national laws. For example, the standard for steel specifications is formulated, and steel mills organize production according to the standard, which can simplify varieties, mass production, and improve quality. Machinery manufacturing factories select steel according to the standard, which can simplify design, process, material supply, and other aspects of work.

In recent years, some departments and enterprises have adopted some parts of the Soviet national standards in production, which has played a certain role, but because our country has not yet established national standards, so the production technology between departments still cannot be well coordinated. The supply of raw materials, the manufacture and use of equipment between departments often occur supply and demand imbalances, making the varieties complex, and the work of trial production of new products is greatly increased, and technical strength is greatly wasted. Take voltage as an example. Our country has inherited voltage levels from various countries, reaching 30-40 kinds (the Soviet Union has only 10 kinds), so power generation, transmission, and use, as well as the manufacture of equipment are much more complicated. Therefore, the promotion of standardization is an important prerequisite for simplifying varieties, improving quality, increasing production, and promoting the cooperation and coordination of production.

The current main problem in promoting standardization is, first of all, to establish a national agency in charge of standards, formulate national standards for our country according to the specific conditions of industrial development, and gradually unify them with reference to Soviet national standards. The method of formulation can be proposed from the bottom up and approved and approved from the top down. Second, various departments of heavy industry should also establish standardization agencies accordingly and gradually promote the standardization work of their own professions. The steps of promotion should start from the main industrial raw materials and main equipment in the heavy industry, first promote the basic standards, and then promote the professional standards.

Third, regarding the planning arrangement, specialization, and cooperation and coordination of heavy industry

Various departments of heavy industry are closely related to each other, and in terms of work arrangement, factory scale, construction speed, and variety development, they must be coordinated and coordinated, otherwise there will be a phenomenon of disconnection. The five-year plan has made appropriate arrangements for these problems, but in the process of implementing the plan, we must also actively adapt to the development of the situation and actively achieve the coordination and connection of annual plans, so as to smoothly complete the five-year plan.

In the heavy industry sector, in addition to state-owned and locally state-owned enterprises, there are also many joint-state and private enterprises. Taking the machinery industry as an example, in 1953, the total production value of modern large-scale machinery industry was 50.5% state-owned, 14.8% locally state-owned, 2.9% joint-state, and 31.8% private. These enterprises should be arranged in a planned manner in terms of production and construction. In the past few years, some capitalists, in pursuit of high profits, have blindly expanded production; some state-owned and locally state-owned enterprises, due to insufficient planned arrangements, have also had the phenomenon of blind development, resulting in repeated varieties, product accumulation, and poor quality, and a great waste of manpower, material resources, and technical strength. In the future, various departments of heavy industry should, based on needs and possibilities, and in accordance with the policy of socialist transformation of private capitalist industry, make more specific arrangements in the plan, so that various types of enterprises can be closely coordinated.

The reasonable arrangement of the plan must be based on specialization and cooperation and coordination. Specialized production is to define the product scope for each enterprise according to the principle of similar products and similar processes. In this way, the enterprise can be proficient in producing technology, quickly develop varieties, adopt specialized high-efficiency equipment, improve processes, organize large-scale or batch production. On the other hand, the products of heavy industry are diverse, the more specialized the production is, the more extensive the cooperation and coordination are needed. Especially in the machinery manufacturing industry, the product structure is complex, such as the factory producing cars and tractors, which needs dozens or even hundreds of factories to cooperate and coordinate. The Soviet Union produces cars and tractors, and the parts supplied by the cooperative and coordinated factories account for more than 50% of the cost of cars and about 30% of the cost of tractors. In our opinion, this level of specialization and cooperation and coordination is already high, but the Soviet Union still thinks it is low, thinking that it affects technological progress and the speed of production development.

Lenin believed that the development of socialized production, the increasing specialization of social labor, and the increasing number of independent industrial departments are one of the most important prerequisites for the socialist mode of production. With the development of heavy industry in our country, a batch of new enterprises will be put into production one after another, and the enterprises will increasingly need to develop in the direction of specialization, and the division of labor and cooperation and coordination will become more extensive and complex, so the work in this aspect will become more important.

In recent years, the state has established and will continue to establish some new industrial departments according to the principle of division of labor, and at the same time, various industrial departments have also defined the professional direction of most enterprises according to the principle of division of labor and organized specialized production, which is completely correct and necessary. However, there are still some factories that have not determined the professional direction, or have determined the professional direction but have not organized specialized production. There are also some factories that emphasize specialized production one-sidedly and do not want to accept cooperative tasks, and even if there is surplus capacity, they do not want to take on odd jobs. There are also some factories that want to make themselves a comprehensive factory, doing everything themselves, requiring the establishment of workshops and the addition of equipment, without considering cooperation and coordination with other factories.

In the future, to further strengthen specialization and cooperation and coordination, the following measures should be taken: first, formulate a long-term variety development plan based on the needs of the state, and thus determine the professional direction of enterprises; second, organize specialized factories according to the principles of need and economic rationality, such as specialized casting, forging, and standard parts factories; third, compile regional cooperation plans and combine departmental cooperation and regional cooperation in a planned manner; fourth, establish systems and set up special agencies to solve various problems in specialization and cooperation and coordination. To implement the above measures, we must also advocate the overall perspective and holistic concept in terms of ideology, and oppose the tendency of localism.

Fourth, improve enterprise management and implement the policy of increasing production and practicing economy to improve labor productivity

During the first five-year plan period, the number of newly built enterprises put into production is not large, and the production plan mainly relies on existing enterprises to complete. Therefore, the technological renovation and improvement of enterprise management of existing enterprises are of great significance. It is wrong to only focus on the construction of new enterprises and not pay attention to the utilization of existing enterprises and not try to bring into play the production capacity of existing enterprises. Experience in recent years has proven that the potential of existing enterprises is still great. As long as we actively learn from the advanced experience of the Soviet Union, accept the rationalization suggestions of the masses, and continuously improve enterprise management, we can greatly improve production capacity. For example, if the backward enterprises in the national flat furnace steel production can reach the production quota of the advanced enterprises, 170,000 tons of steel can be increased annually, accounting for 6.5% of the current production.

The management work of various departments of heavy industry has been greatly improved in recent years, but there are still many shortcomings. As Vice Premier Li Fuchun pointed out, many enterprises have only completed the output value indicators, but have not completed the variety and quality indicators of products, and have not completed the indicators of improving labor productivity and reducing costs; in the formulation of production plans, the requirements for output value and quantity are relatively clear and strict, while the variety, quality, and cost are not paid much attention to. Taking steel as an example, everyone pays attention to the tonnage and output value, but pays less attention to the production of new varieties; taking the machinery manufacturing industry as an example, in the calculation of completing the state tasks, it is often also based on the quantity and output value of the machinery, parts, and components produced, not based on the variety, quantity, and quality of the machinery, parts, and components produced for unified accounting. The phenomenon of loose and tight production in the middle of the month is still very common, and many enterprises only complete 20% of the monthly plan in the first ten days, 30% in the middle ten days, and 50% in the last ten days. The phenomenon of waste in production is also very serious: the metal utilization rate of our country's machinery and equipment manufacturing is only 45.5%, while the metal utilization rate in the Soviet Union's machinery manufacturing industry is 60-80%. There are too many non-production personnel, by the end of 1954, the proportion of non-production personnel in the enterprises under the three departments of heavy industry, fuel industry, and first machinery industry had risen to 26%. The equipment utilization rate is very low, the actual operating hours of cutting machine tools and forging and pressing equipment throughout the year still do not reach 60% of the hours that should be operated. The labor quota is not advanced, and many enterprises still use the method of estimated labor or experience statistics quota, so they cannot reflect the achievements of advanced workers and improve labor productivity. The work of implementing piecework wages is also very slow.

To overcome the above shortcomings, in addition to the previous mention of adopting and mastering new technologies, we must also strengthen planning work and economic work to improve labor productivity and economic results, and ensure the full completion of the state plan and the tasks of increasing production and practicing economy. First, we must overcome various causes of unbalanced production, strive to achieve balanced production, reduce non-production hours, actively eliminate overtime, prevent equipment accidents and personal accidents, and strengthen labor discipline. Second, we should better utilize the existing production area, increase the operating hours of machines, improve the equipment utilization rate, fully bring into play the production capacity, and oppose the tendency to easily abandon the existing equipment. Third, we should improve the quota work, gradually adopt advanced economic and technical quotas to improve the advanced nature of the plan. Improve the wage work so that the wage policy can promote the continuous improvement of labor productivity. Fourth, we should vigorously reduce the industrial administrative organs and non-production personnel, strengthen the production units. Fifth, we should strengthen economic activity analysis and accounting supervision, and through the comprehensive examination of plan indicators to expose shortcomings, expose waste, and expose subjectivism and bureaucracy in the leadership work of enterprises.

Fifth, regarding the training of technical personnel

The scale of heavy industry is gradually expanding, and new enterprises are being put into production one after another, all of which require technical personnel. In the past few years, although the growth rate of technical personnel is not small, it still cannot keep up with the needs. The current situation of technical personnel is: the number is not enough, the types of workers are unbalanced, and the technical level is not high. The average technical personnel of various departments of heavy industry only account for 5.7% of the total number of production workers; there are more low-level workers among the production workers, and there are not enough high-level workers and special workers, and the average technical level of workers is only 3.2-3.5 levels, while the new enterprises designed by the Soviet Union for our country generally require an average of 4 levels or above. Due to the lack of technical personnel, the increase in new products is still not fast enough, the quality of products is not good enough, new enterprises and new equipment cannot be quickly mastered, and technical research work cannot be quickly carried out. Therefore, training and strengthening the technical force is a key problem that must be solved at present, and in the future, we should: improve the quality of school education, and plan to send personnel to study abroad; strengthen the part-time education of workers, and pay attention to organizing the learning of technology by transferred senior and middle-level cadres, and improve their business leadership capabilities; rationally use the existing technical personnel, strengthen their political and ideological education, and through the establishment of scientific and technological research institutions, cultivate scientific and technological talents.

The above are the main problems that the heavy industry sector must solve during the five-year plan. Due to our weak foundation and lack of experience, solving these problems will encounter many difficulties. However, we have the help of the Soviet Union and other people's democratic countries, and the high enthusiasm for construction of the broad masses of workers, technical personnel, and cadres. As long as we seriously learn from the advanced experience of the Soviet Union and other people's democratic countries, do a good job in the political and ideological work of enterprises, and combine political and ideological work with economic work well, give full play to the enthusiasm and creativity of the masses, the tasks of heavy industry in the five-year plan will definitely be completed.

In the heavy construction work, we must also maintain a high degree of revolutionary vigilance. Counter-revolutionaries are extremely hostile to our country's industrial construction, and heavy industry is the lifeline of the country's economy and the foundation of industrialization. They will first sabotage heavy industry. The events of the Hu Feng counter-revolutionary group and the Pan Hannian treason case, as well as other sabotage incidents, have already sounded the alarm for us. Therefore, all of us in the heavy industry sector must, while working hard in construction, also learn to fight against all enemies and resolutely eliminate hidden counter-revolutionaries to protect the achievements of our country's heavy industry construction.

Comrades, the first five-year plan for the development of the national economy of our country has been formulated. Let us, under the banner of Mao Zedong, together with the people of the whole country and all the workers, strive for the victory and over-fulfillment of this great five-year plan!

    æœºæ¢°å·¥ä¸šçš„è¿™ç§æŠ€æœ¯è½åŽçŠ¶å†µï¼Œæ˜¾ç„¶æ˜¯å’Œå‘å±•å›½æ°‘ç»æµŽçš„è¦æ±‚ä¸ç›¸é€‚åº”çš„ã€‚ä¸å»ºç«‹ä¸€ä¸ªå¼ºå¤§çš„æœºæ¢°å·¥ä¸šï¼Œå°±ä¸èƒ½å®žçŽ°ç¤¾ä¼šä¸»ä¹‰å·¥ä¸šåŒ–ï¼Œä¸èƒ½ç‹¬ç«‹åœ°å‘å±•å›½æ°‘ç»æµŽï¼Œå› æ­¤ï¼Œç¬¬ä¸€ä¸ªäº”å¹´è®¡åˆ’æŠŠå‘å±•é‡å·¥ä¸šä½œä¸ºç¤¾ä¼šä¸»ä¹‰å·¥ä¸šåŒ–çš„ä¸­å¿ƒçŽ¯èŠ‚ï¼Œå¹¶å¼ºè°ƒå‘å±•æœºæ¢°å·¥ä¸šï¼Œæ˜¯å®Œå…¨å¿…è¦çš„ã€‚æŽå¯Œæ˜¥å‰¯æ€»ç†åœ¨äº”å¹´è®¡åˆ’çš„æŠ¥å‘Šä¸­æŒ‡å‡ºï¼šæé«˜å·¥ä¸šæŠ€æœ¯æ°´å¹³ï¼Œæ˜¯å®Œæˆç¤¾ä¼šä¸»ä¹‰å·¥ä¸šåŒ–çš„ä»»åŠ¡çš„ä¸€ä¸ªåŸºæœ¬æ¡ä»¶ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬è®¤ä¸ºè¿™æ˜¯å®Œå…¨æ­£ç¡®çš„ã€‚å¿…é¡»å…‹æœæœºæ¢°å·¥ä¸šçš„æŠ€æœ¯è½åŽçŠ¶å†µï¼Œæ‰èƒ½ä½¿æœºæ¢°å·¥ä¸šå¼ºå¤§åœ°å‘å±•èµ·æ¥ã€‚

    äº”å¹´è®¡åˆ’ä¸­ï¼Œæœºæ¢°å·¥ä¸šå°†å»ºè®¾ä¸€æ‰¹æ–°çš„å·¥åŽ‚ï¼Œè¿™äº›å·¥åŽ‚éƒ½æ˜¯ç”¨æœ€æ–°æŠ€æœ¯è£…å¤‡èµ·æ¥çš„ï¼Œå»ºæˆåŽï¼Œå°†å¤§å¤§æ”¹å˜æœºæ¢°å·¥ä¸šçš„é¢è²Œã€‚è¿™æ˜¯å…‹æœæœºæ¢°å·¥ä¸šæŠ€æœ¯è½åŽçŠ¶æ€æœ€é‡è¦çš„ä¸€ä¸ªæ–¹é¢ã€‚æ–°å·¥åŽ‚å»ºæˆä»¥åŽï¼Œå…³é”®é—®é¢˜æ˜¯æŽŒæ¡æ–°æŠ€æœ¯é—®é¢˜ï¼ŒæŽŒæ¡äº†æ–°æŠ€æœ¯æ‰èƒ½åˆ¶é€ å‡ºåˆæ ¼çš„äº§å“ï¼Œå‘æŒ¥å·¥åŽ‚çš„ç”Ÿäº§èƒ½åŠ›ï¼Œè¾¾åˆ°å·¥åŽ‚è®¾è®¡çš„è¦æ±‚ã€‚è¦æŽŒæ¡æ–°æŠ€æœ¯ï¼Œé¦–å…ˆï¼Œåœ¨å¼€å·¥å‰è¦åšå¥½å„é¡¹å‡†å¤‡å·¥ä½œã€‚å›½å¤–è®¾è®¡çš„åŽ‚ï¼Œå½“å„ç§æŠ€æœ¯èµ„æ–™åˆ°åŽ‚ä»¥åŽï¼Œå°±è¦è¿…é€Ÿç»„ç»‡ç¿»è¯‘ï¼Œè®¤çœŸå­¦ä¹ ï¼Œè€ŒåŽä»¥è¿™äº›èµ„æ–™ä¸ºæ ¹æ®ï¼Œè¿›è¡Œå„æ–¹é¢çš„å…·ä½“å‡†å¤‡å·¥ä½œã€‚å¦‚äººå‘˜ã€è®¾å¤‡ã€å·¥å…·ã€ææ–™ã€åŽ‚å¤–åä½œç­‰ã€‚è¿™äº›å‡†å¤‡å·¥ä½œï¼Œéƒ½è¦ä¾ç…§æŠ€æœ¯èµ„æ–™ä¸­æ‰€è§„å®šçš„æ¡ä»¶ï¼Œåœ¨å¼€å·¥å‰å‡†å¤‡é½å…¨ã€‚å…¶æ¬¡ï¼Œè¦è¿›è¡Œè¯•ç”Ÿäº§ï¼šè€ƒéªŒè®¾å¤‡ã€å·¥å…·ã€ææ–™ç­‰æ˜¯å¦ç¬¦åˆè¦æ±‚ï¼Œæ ¡å¯¹å„ç§æŠ€æœ¯æ–‡ä»¶ï¼Œå¹¶æ•™è‚²èŒå·¥ç†Ÿæ‚‰å’ŒæŽŒæ¡æ–°è®¾å¤‡ã€å·¥å…·åŠæ“ä½œæ–¹æ³•ç­‰ã€‚åœ¨è¯•ç”Ÿäº§ä¸­ä»Žé›¶ä»¶åˆ°æˆå“éƒ½å…ˆè¦æ±‚æŒ‰è§„çŸ©åšæˆï¼ˆè¾¾åˆ°è´¨é‡æ ‡å‡†ï¼‰ï¼Œç„¶åŽè¦æ±‚åšå¿«ï¼ˆè¾¾åˆ°æŠ€æœ¯å®šé¢ï¼‰ï¼Œç›´åˆ°æ‰€æœ‰è¿‡ç¨‹éƒ½è¢«æŽŒæ¡äº†ï¼Œæ‰ç®—å®Œå…¨æŽŒæ¡äº†æ–°çš„ç”Ÿäº§ã€‚

    ç¬¬ä¸€ä¸ªäº”å¹´è®¡åˆ’ä¹Ÿè¯¦å°½åœ°è¯´æ˜Žäº†å…³äºŽå¦‚ä½•è§£å†³å°å†œç»æµŽåŒç¤¾ä¼šä¸»ä¹‰å·¥ä¸šåŒ–ä¹‹é—´çš„çŸ›ç›¾ã€‚åŒæ—¶ä¹Ÿè¯¦å°½åœ°è¯´æ˜Žäº†å…³äºŽå¦‚ä½•è§£å†³èµ„æœ¬ä¸»ä¹‰ç»æµŽå’Œç¤¾ä¼šä¸»ä¹‰ç»æµŽä¹‹é—´çš„çŸ›ç›¾ã€‚è¿™äº›è¯´æ˜Žå’Œè§„å®šï¼Œæ­£æ˜¾ç¤ºäº†æˆ‘ä»¬çš„ç¬¬ä¸€ä¸ªäº”å¹´è®¡åˆ’æ˜¯å¤šä¹ˆå…¨é¢å¤šä¹ˆæ­£ç¡®çš„ä¸€ä¸ªä¼Ÿå¤§çš„ç»æµŽå»ºè®¾è®¡åˆ’ï¼Œè¿™ä¸€ä¼Ÿå¤§ç»æµŽå»ºè®¾è®¡åˆ’çš„å®žè¡Œï¼Œæ ‡å¿—ç€æˆ‘ä»¬ä¼Ÿå¤§çš„ç¥–å›½çš„å‰é€”æœ‰æ— é™çš„å…‰æ˜Žå¹¸ç¦å’Œç¾Žå¥½çš„è¿œæ™¯ã€‚

    ç”±æ­¤å¯è§ï¼šå›½å®¶çš„ç²®é£Ÿç»Ÿè´­ç»Ÿé”€æ”¿ç­–æ˜¯å®Œå…¨æ­£ç¡®çš„ã€‚è‡³äºŽå¹¿ä¸œç²®é£Ÿç»Ÿé”€ä¸Šä¸€åº¦å‡ºçŽ°çš„ç´§å¼ æƒ…å†µï¼Œåˆ™æ˜¯æˆ‘ä»¬å·¥ä½œä¸Šçš„é”™è¯¯å’Œç¼ºç‚¹é€ æˆçš„ã€‚å¦‚æžœæˆ‘ä»¬åœ¨åŽ»å¹´ç»Ÿè´­ç»Ÿé”€å·¥ä½œä¸Šæ²¡æœ‰å‰æ¾åŽç´§çš„çŽ°è±¡ï¼Œä»Šå¹´ä¸€æœˆä»½ä»¥åŽçš„ç»Ÿé”€å·¥ä½œæŠ“å¾—ç´§ï¼Œè€Œå››æœˆä»½ä»¥åŽåˆä¸æ˜¯é‡‡å–çŒ›ç„¶åŽ‹é”€çš„åŠžæ³•ï¼ˆå¯ä»¥è‚¯å®šå››æœˆä»½å¦‚ä¸é‡‡å–åŽ‹é”€åŠžæ³•ï¼Œæœ€å¤šè¶…é”€ä¸€äº¿æ–¤å¤§ç±³ï¼Œè¿™åœ¨å¹¿ä¸œå½“å‰ç²®é£Ÿæƒ…å†µè¯´æ¥æ˜¯å¯ä»¥è´Ÿæ‹…çš„ï¼‰ï¼Œé‚£æœ«å››äº”æœˆé—´çš„ç´§å¼ çŽ°è±¡å°±å®Œå…¨å¯ä»¥é¿å…ã€‚è¿™æ˜¯å¹¿ä¸œå…¨çœæžæ·±åˆ»çš„æ•™è®­ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬å·²ç»ç»“åˆâ€œä¸‰å®šâ€å·¥ä½œï¼Œåšå†³äºˆä»¥çº æ­£ã€‚æŒ‰ç…§ç›®å‰ç¬¬ä¸€æ‰¹å·²å®Œæˆâ€œä¸‰å®šâ€çš„ä¹¡çš„æƒ…å†µçœ‹æ¥ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬æœ‰ä¿¡å¿ƒæŠŠç²®é£Ÿå·¥ä½œåšå¥½ã€‚ç²®é£Ÿç»Ÿè´­ç»Ÿé”€æ”¿ç­–æ˜¯å›½å®¶åœ¨è¿‡æ¸¡æ—¶æœŸçš„æ ¹æœ¬æŽªæ–½ä¹‹ä¸€ï¼Œæ˜¯ä¸èƒ½æœ‰ä¸æ¯«åŠ¨æ‘‡çš„ï¼Œè‡³äºŽæˆ‘ä»¬å·¥ä½œä¸­çš„ç¼ºç‚¹å’Œé”™è¯¯åˆ™æ˜¯å¿…é¡»åšå†³çº æ­£çš„ã€‚ç›®å‰åé©å‘½åˆ†å­çŒ–ç—çš„ç ´åæ´»åŠ¨ï¼Œæ˜¯å€¼å¾—æˆ‘ä»¬ä¸¥é‡è­¦æƒ•çš„ã€‚æˆ‘ä»¬å®Œå…¨æ‹¥æŠ¤å¸¸åŠ¡å§”å‘˜ä¼šæ‰¹å‡†å°†åé©å‘½åˆ†å­æ½˜æ±‰å¹´ã€èƒ¡é£Žé€®æ•å®¡åˆ¤çš„æŽªæ–½ã€‚å¹¿ä¸œåœ°å¤„å›½é˜²å‰çº¿ï¼Œæ•Œæƒ…æ˜¯ä¸¥é‡çš„ã€‚æ—¥å¤œåŒå…¬å¼€çš„å’Œéšè”½çš„æ•Œäººæ–—äº‰ç€çš„å¹¿ä¸œäººæ°‘ï¼Œæ·±åˆ»åœ°ä½“ä¼šåˆ°åŠ å¼ºå›½é˜²åŠ›é‡ã€åŠ å¼ºé•‡åŽ‹åé©å‘½å·¥ä½œçš„ä¸¥é‡æ„ä¹‰ã€‚ä¸€å¹´æ¥ç”±äºŽæˆ‘ä»¬å¯¹é•‡åå·¥ä½œæ²¡æœ‰æŠ“ç´§ï¼Œåé©å‘½åˆ†å­å’Œå„ç§ååˆ†å­ååˆ†åš£å¼ ï¼Œæ•Œäººæ‰€è¿›è¡Œçš„å‡¶æ€ã€ç ´åã€é€ è°£ã€è¯¬è”‘äº‹ä»¶å±‚å‡ºä¸ç©·ï¼Œå¹¿å·žå¸‚åŠå…¶ä»–å„åŸŽå¸‚çš„åˆ‘äº‹æ¡ˆä»¶æ¯”é‡ä¹Ÿå¤§ä¸ºå¢žåŠ ï¼Œä¸¥é‡å¨èƒåˆ°å¹¿ä¸œçš„ç¤¾ä¼šæ²»å®‰ã€ç»æµŽå»ºè®¾å’Œç¥–å›½å—éƒ¨å›½é˜²çš„å·©å›ºã€‚å› æ­¤ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬è¦è¿…é€Ÿæ”¹æ­£å·¥ä½œä¸­çš„ç¼ºç‚¹ï¼Œæ›´ç´§å¯†åœ°å›¢ç»“å…¨çœäººæ°‘åšå†³åœ°å‘å…¬å¼€çš„å’Œæš—è—çš„åé©å‘½åˆ†å­ä½œæ–—äº‰ï¼ŒæŠŠä»–ä»¬å½»åº•æ¶ˆç­å¹²å‡€ï¼Œå·©å›ºæµ·é˜²è¾¹é˜²ï¼Œä¸ºä¿å«ä¼Ÿå¤§ç¥–å›½çš„ç¤¾ä¼šä¸»ä¹‰å»ºè®¾äº‹ä¸šçš„é¡ºåˆ©è¿›è¡Œè€Œå¥‹æ–—åˆ°åº•ï¼

    åœ¨é‡å·¥ä¸šéƒ¨é—¨ä¸­ï¼Œé™¤å›½è¥ã€åœ°æ–¹å›½è¥ä¼ä¸šå¤–ï¼Œè¿˜æœ‰å¾ˆå¤šå…¬ç§åˆè¥å’Œç§è¥ä¼ä¸šã€‚ä»¥æœºæ¢°å·¥ä¸šä¸ºä¾‹ï¼Œä¸€ä¹äº”ä¸‰å¹´çŽ°ä»£å¤§åž‹æœºæ¢°å·¥ä¸šçš„ç”Ÿäº§æ€»å€¼ä¸­ï¼Œå›½è¥å ç™¾åˆ†ä¹‹äº”åç‚¹äº”ï¼Œåœ°æ–¹å›½è¥å ç™¾åˆ†ä¹‹åå››ç‚¹å…«ï¼Œå…¬ç§åˆè¥å ç™¾åˆ†ä¹‹äºŒç‚¹ä¹ï¼Œç§è¥å ç™¾åˆ†ä¹‹ä¸‰åä¸€ç‚¹å…«ã€‚è¿™äº›ä¼ä¸šåœ¨ç”Ÿäº§å’Œå»ºè®¾ä¸Šï¼Œåº”åšåˆ°ç»Ÿç­¹å®‰æŽ’ã€‚ä»¥å¾€å‡ å¹´ä¸­ï¼Œæœ‰äº›èµ„æœ¬å®¶ä¸ºäº†è¿½æ±‚é«˜é¢åˆ©æ¶¦ï¼Œæ›¾ç›²ç›®æ‰©å¤§ç”Ÿäº§ï¼›æŸäº›å›½è¥å’Œåœ°æ–¹å›½è¥ä¼ä¸šï¼Œå› ç»Ÿç­¹å®‰æŽ’ä¸å¤Ÿï¼Œä¹Ÿæœ‰ç›²ç›®å‘å±•çš„çŽ°è±¡ï¼Œå› è€Œé€ æˆå“ç§é‡å¤ã€äº§å“ç§¯åŽ‹ã€è´¨é‡ä½ŽåŠ£ï¼Œåœ¨ç‰©åŠ›ã€è´¢åŠ›ã€æŠ€æœ¯åŠ›é‡ä¸Šéƒ½æµªè´¹å¾ˆå¤§ã€‚ä»ŠåŽé‡å·¥ä¸šå„éƒ¨é—¨åœ¨æ‰§è¡Œäº”å¹´è®¡åˆ’çš„è¿‡ç¨‹ä¸­ï¼Œåº”ä»Žéœ€è¦å’Œå¯èƒ½å‡ºå‘ï¼Œå¹¶ä¾ç…§å¯¹ç§äººèµ„æœ¬ä¸»ä¹‰å·¥ä¸šçš„ç¤¾ä¼šä¸»ä¹‰æ”¹é€ æ–¹é’ˆï¼Œåœ¨è®¡åˆ’ä¸Šåšæ›´å…·ä½“åœ°å®‰æŽ’ï¼Œä½¿å„ç±»ä¼ä¸šå¯†åˆ‡é…åˆã€‚

    åˆ—å®è®¤ä¸ºï¼šç”Ÿäº§ç¤¾ä¼šåŒ–çš„å‘å±•ï¼Œç¤¾ä¼šåŠ³åŠ¨çš„æ—¥ç›Šä¸“é—¨åŒ–ï¼Œå’Œç‹¬ç«‹å·¥ä¸šéƒ¨é—¨çš„æ—¥ç›Šå¢žåŠ ï¼Œæ˜¯ç¤¾ä¼šä¸»ä¹‰ç”Ÿäº§æ–¹å¼çš„æœ€é‡è¦å‰æä¹‹ä¸€ã€‚éšç€æˆ‘å›½é‡å·¥ä¸šçš„å‘å±•ï¼Œä¸€æ‰¹ä¸€æ‰¹æ–°ä¼ä¸šæŠ•å…¥ç”Ÿäº§ï¼Œä¼ä¸šæ—¥ç›Šéœ€è¦å‘ç€ä¸“ä¸šåŒ–çš„æ–¹å‘å‘å±•ï¼Œä¸“ä¸šåˆ†å·¥å’Œåä½œé…åˆå¿…å°†æ›´åŠ å¹¿æ³›å’Œå¤æ‚ï¼Œå› è€ŒåŠ å¼ºè¿™æ–¹é¢çš„å·¥ä½œæ„ˆç›Šé‡è¦ã€‚
